CHAPTER 4

Core Layer

In this chapter, we will see how to develop Core Layer that is in  
charge of business logic. We will validate HTTP Request ﬁelds  
and see how can we manipulate system resources in order to

simulate real-world usage.


Structure

In this chapter, we will discuss the following topics:

Null String

Core Layer – Business Logic

User functions

Book functions


Objectives

After studying this unit, you should be able to:

Know how to handle required and optional request ﬁelds.

Learn how to create Core Layer of server application.


4.1 Null string

When we ﬁll some form on a website we often have required

ﬁelds (usually marked with asterisk *) and optional ﬁelds. For  
example, when we ﬁll registration form on some forum,  
username, password and full name can be required, but mobile

number and address can be optional. You can ﬁll them, if you  
want, but you can create account without them.

Core Layer will validate and prepare all ﬁelds from request  
(required and optional) and send it to the Data Layer. If we use

relational database (as we will do in our application) we will have  
column for optional ﬁelds. Here we have one small problem.  
How to write optional ﬁeld?

We have two options, we can write default value (0 for numbers

and empty string for strings) or we can write NULL. In  
databases, NULL represents the absence of value, and 0 or empty  
string have a certain value. So here we will use NULL approach.  
Now we can easily create queries that will return (in our  
application) all books without description.

In some SQL implementations, NULL will allocate less memory  
than empty string. But that is out of scope for this book.

We must also point out one big disadvantage of this approach.

We already mentioned that NULL is a value, so we cannot use


regular operators as we can use for values. We must use NULL

dedicated operators. These two expressions should have the same  
result, true.

“” = “”  
NULL = NULL

First expression will be true, but the second one will return  
unknown. In order to compare with NULL, we must use IS NULL  
instead of equal operator.

Now when we are familiar with NULL problem, we can do GO  
implementation of Null String. We will create new ﬁle nullString.go  
in util folder. Go already has implementation for this NullString  
in SQL package, so we will use it for our implementation.

Why would we create our own implementation? In order to use  
NullString from SQL package we must include package We will  
NullString implementation in every server application that we  
develop. So we can move NullString implementation in special  
project, called modules, and we can include that project in all  
other server applications. This way we will include in only one  
place.

A NullString struct have two ﬁelds, String and Value. If String is  
not NULL, Valid will be true. So ﬁrst we will create our own  
struct with only one ﬁeld of type NullString from SQL package.

// NullString represents nullable string.


// Intended for use in fetching data from SQL queries  
type NullString struct {  
sql.NullString  
}

Now we need two functions, ﬁrst will be used to create NullString

depending on the passing optional parameter. The second will be  
used to return value from

var (  
// NewNullableString return a null String if the parameter is  
empty,  
// a valid String otherwise  
NewNullableString = newNullableString

// GetNullStringValue returns empty string if null.String is null,  
// a valid String otherwise

GetNullStringValue = getNullStringValue  
)

Now let us take a look of implementation of newNullableString()  
function. When blank optional ﬁeld (empty string) is passed,  
NULL will be created. We can describe NULL as where String has

a value NULL and Valid has a value false. If provided optional  
ﬁeld has a value (non-empty string), String will have a value of  
provided ﬁeld value and value true will be assigned to

func newNullableString(x string) NullString {

if x == "" {


return NullString{}  
}

return NullString{sql.NullString{String: x, Valid: true}}  
}

Second function getNullStringValue() will return empty string if

Value ﬁeld of provided NullString has value false, otherwise it will  
return value of String ﬁeld.

func getNullStringValue(x NullString) string {  
if x.Valid == false {  
return ""  
}

return x.String  
}

We see usage of NullString in this chapter. Go also have support  
for nullable numbers.


4.2 Core Layer – Business Logic

Core Layer will handle business logic. Business logic will simulate

usage of system resource and determine how they will be created,  
stored, and changed. Core Layer will call only operations from  
Data Layer.

We will adopt naming convention for ﬁles in core folder. It is

good practice to name ﬁles by functionality. In our application we  
will have two ﬁles, user.go and In the ﬁrst ﬁle, we will put all  
functions that operate with users. All book functions will be put

in the second ﬁle.

We also had another option. We separate core functions by API  
type. We can put all Core Layer functions called in handleOpen()  
function from Handler Layer in ﬁle called In that fashion we can

put all functions of Core Layer called in handleMember() and  
handleLibrerian() in ﬁles member.go and librarian.go respectively.  
Our application is quite simple so we will use ﬁrst option.


4.2.1 User functions

We have two user functions. One for user login and another one

for user authentication.

var (  
// Login will return user's auth token  
Login = login

// AuthorizeUser returns user's role if user token exists  
// if token not exists, empty string will be returned  
AuthorizeUser = authorizeUser

)

First function, login will try to ﬁnd user with username and  
password provided in HTTP Request Body. If user with provided  
username and password exist in system function will return

authentication token for that user. Token will be used in HTTP  
Request Header for Member and Liberian API.

First, we will use json package to decode (convert) JSON from  
HTTP Request Body to Go struct loginRequest. It is important to  
use same names for struct and JSON ﬁelds.

We must validate provided ﬁelds. We do not need to do that  
invalid ﬁelds can be detected during execution of database query  
but it is good practice to prevent execution of query with invalid


parameters. Database is bottleneck of the system so we must try

to prevent all unnecessary database operations.

We will use some standard for errors. When JSON decoding or  
validation fails ErrBadRequest will be returned. When Data Layer  
function returns zero (default) value (empty string, zero or nil)  
ErrResourceNotFound will be returned. When execution of Data  
Layer function fails it means that some unhanded situation  
occurred so we will return

In this case, we can only check if provider username or password

is empty string. Function TrimSpace() from strings package will  
remove all leading white spaces. When everything is ready we can  
call LoginUser() from Data Layer.

func login(ctx context.Context, requestBody io.Reader)  
(response interface{}, err error) {

type loginRequest struct {  
Username string  
Password string  
}

request := &loginRequest{}  
err = json.NewDecoder(requestBody).Decode(request)  
if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to decode JSON"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInvalidJSONBody,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)


return  
}  
request.Username = strings.TrimSpace(request.Username)  
request.Password = strings.TrimSpace(request.Password)  
if request.Username == "" || request.Password == "" {  
cause := "Username or password are empty"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}  
token, err := data.LoginUser(ctx, request.Username,

request.Password)  
if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to login user"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,  
err)  
return  
}

if token == "" {  
cause := "Invalid username or password"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInvalidCredentials,  
util.ErrNotAuthenticated, err)  
return  
}

type loginResponse struct {  
Token string  
}

response = &loginResponse{


Token: token,  
}  
return  
}

If Data Layer return empty string, there is no user with provided  
username and password, so we must return error to client. If  
non-empty string is returned we will prepare response and return  
it to client.

If we use some struct only in one place in code, like loginRequest  
and loginResponse in this function, we can deﬁne that struct  
inside the body of function where struct will be used. If we use  
some struct in only one ﬁle we can deﬁne struct at the start of  
the ﬁle, such struct will not be exported so it can start with  
lowercase.

The second function, will return the user role for provided  
authentication token. This function is used in Handler Layer to  
check if user has a proper role to call certain API.

In this function, we must check returned role. Inside values folder  
we will create consts.go ﬁle. We will put all system constants  
here.

// Values for user role  
const (  
UserRoleUnknown = 0  
UserRoleMember = 1


UserRoleLibrarian = 2  
)

We will assign an integer value for each role. Unknown role  
(value 0) will be considered as an error.

Function will have similar ﬂow as First, we will validate provided  
token, then we will call AuthorizeUser() from Data Layer. If Data  
Layer return Unknown user role (value 0) we will return error to  
client. If returned value is valid we will prepare response and  
send it to client.

func authorizeUser(ctx context.Context, token string)  
(response int, err error) {

token = strings.TrimSpace(token)  
if token == "" {  
cause := "Invalid value for token parameter"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}

userRole, err := data.AuthorizeUser(ctx, token)

if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to authorize user"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,  
err)

return


}  
if userRole == values.UserRoleUnknown {  
cause := "User not found"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,  
util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)  
return  
}  
response = int(userRole)  
return  
}


4.2.2 Book functions

In book.go ﬁle, we will have set of functions for manipulation of

book resource. We can create new book, get list of books (this  
will be diﬀerent, depending on the user role), get single book,  
update book, delete book and borrow/return book.

var (

// CreateBook creates new Book  
CreateBook = createBook

// GetBook returns book  
GetBook = getBook

// GetAllBooks returns list of books  
GetAllBooks = getAllBooks

// UpdateBook updates book  
UpdateBook = updateBook

// DeleteBook deletes book

DeleteBook = deleteBook

// BorrowOrReturnBook borrows book if is available  
// or returns book if is borrowed  
BorrowOrReturnBook = borrowOrReturnBook


)

As we have seen on the example of user functions, Core Layer

functions are similar, so we will just point out only details that  
we have not seen before.

A createBook() function will create new book. Here, we have one  
optional ﬁeld, We do not need to validate optional ﬁelds, if they  
are not provided they will have default value (0 or empty string,  
depends on data type), so we just need to convert them to  
nullable type. We will convert Description to nullable string during

Data Layer function call.

An error (which is not validation error) only can occur during  
execution of Data Layer function. It can only be some kind of  
internal error so we will handle that situation.

func createBook(ctx context.Context, requestBody io.Reader)

(response interface{}, err error) {  
type createBookRequest struct {  
BookName string

AuthorName string  
Publisher string  
Description string  
}

request := &createBookRequest{}  
err = json.NewDecoder(requestBody).Decode(request)


if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to decode JSON"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInvalidJSONBody,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}

request.BookName = strings.TrimSpace(request.BookName)  
if request.BookName == "" {  
cause := "Trying to create book with empty name"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}

request.AuthorName = strings.TrimSpace(request.AuthorName)  
if request.AuthorName == "" {

cause := "Trying to create book with empty author name"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}

request.Publisher = strings.TrimSpace(request.Publisher)  
if request.Publisher == "" {  
cause := "Trying to create book with empty publisher"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}


response, err = data.CreateBook(ctx, request.BookName,  
request.AuthorName, request.Publisher,  
util.NewNullableString(request.Description))  
if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to create book"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,  
err)  
return  
}  
return  
}

In getBook() function, after Data Layer function call we will check  
returned value. If we provided non-existent bookID returned value  
will be equal to nil and we will return

func getBook(ctx context.Context, bookID string)  
response interface{}, err error) {

if bookID == "" {  
cause := "Invalid value for bookID parameter"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return  
}

book, err := data.GetBook(ctx, bookID)  
if err != nil {


cause := "Failed to get book"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,  
err)

return  
}

if book == nil {  
cause := "Book not found"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,  
util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)  
return  
}

response = book  
return  
}

Next function getAllBooks() it’s interesting than others. First, we  
will give explanations for parameters. First parameter searchTerm  
is a word or phrase we will use to match with book name, for  
example, if we want to see list of all encyclopedias we will send  
as value for

Empty string is valid value for search term. If we compare book  
names with empty string, all book names will match search  
criteria, because empty string is part of all strings.

Next two parameters, rowOﬀset and will be used for pagination.  
Pagination is process of dividing a result set (list of books in our  
case) to discrete pages. The ﬁrst pagination parameter rowLimit  
represents number of books returned in one The second


pagination parameter represents number of books we wish to  
before selecting the ﬁrst one for the

Let us see this on simple example. Let us’ assume that we have  
30 books and we want to divide them to three ten book pages.  
All pages will have the same rowLimit value 10. First page will  
contain ﬁrst ten books so we must start from start and we don’t  
need to skip any books, so rowOﬀset will have a value 0.

Next page will contain books from eleven to twenty. We must  
start from position 11. To do that we must skip the ﬁrst ten  
book, so rowOﬀset will have a value 10. The last page will  
contain books from 21 to 30. We must skip ﬁrst twenty books so  
rowOﬀset will have a value 20.

Now it’s obvious that if we set rowLimit to 0, we will divide list  
of book to pages of size 0. This is not very useful so we must  
validate this value. If invalid value is provided we will set it to

value that we deﬁned in consts.go ﬁle in values folder.

Result will be diﬀerent for User and Librarian. User will see only  
available books, librarians will see all books with information who

borrowed which book. Depending on user role diﬀerent Data  
Layer function will be called.

We must return list of books with all parameters, so that client

knows how to display and reconstruct the whole book list.

Usually on web pages and phone apps we have arrows to move


to next or previous page. This action can trigger API with proper

pagination parameters.

func getAllBooks(ctx context.Context, searchTerm string, rowOﬀset,  
rowLimit, userRole int) (response interface{}, err error) {

if rowOﬀset < 0 {  
cause := "Invalid value for row oﬀser parameter"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)

return  
}

if rowLimit < 0 || rowLimit > values.MaxRowLimit {

cause := "Invalid value for row limit parameter"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return

}

if rowLimit == 0 {  
rowLimit = values.MaxRowLimit

}

var books interface{}

if userRole == values.UserRoleMember {

books, err = data.GetAllBooksForMember(ctx, searchTerm,  
rowOﬀset, rowLimit)

} else {  
books, err = data.GetAllBooksForLibrerian(ctx, searchTerm,

rowOﬀset, rowLimit)  
}


if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to get all books"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)  
return

}

type metaData struct {  
SearchTerm string `json:",omitempty"`

RowOﬀset int `json:",omitempty"`  
RowLimit int

}

meta := &metaData{  
SearchTerm: searchTerm,

RowOﬀset: rowOﬀset,  
RowLimit: rowLimit,

}

type getAllResponse struct {  
Data interface{} `json:"data"`

Meta interface{} `json:"meta"`  
}

response = &getAllResponse{

Data: books,  
Meta: meta,

}


return

}

It is good practice to have two ﬁelds for each resource of our  
system, two timestamps, time when resource is created and last

update time. When update function from Data Layer returns  
invalid date (January 1, 2001), we will know that resource not

exists in our system and we will return error to client.

func updateBook(ctx context.Context, requestBody io.Reader)  
(response interface{}, err error) {

type updateBookRequest struct {

BookID string  
BookName string

AuthorName string  
Publisher string

Description string  
}

request := &updateBookRequest{}

err = json.NewDecoder(requestBody).Decode(request)  
if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to decode JSON"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInvalidJSONBody,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return

}


request.BookID = strings.TrimSpace(request.BookID)

if request.BookID == "" {  
cause := "Invalid value for bookID parameter"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,  
util.ErrBadRequest, err)

return  
}

request.BookName = strings.TrimSpace(request.BookName)

if request.BookName == "" {  
cause := "Invalid value for book name"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation, u

til.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return

}

request.AuthorName = strings.TrimSpace(request.AuthorName)  
if request.AuthorName == "" {

cause := "Invalid value for author name"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)  
return

}

request.Publisher = strings.TrimSpace(request.Publisher)  
if request.Publisher == "" {

cause := "Invalid value for publisher"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)


return

}

updatedAt, err := data.UpdateBook(ctx, request.BookID,  
request.BookName, request.AuthorName, request.Publisher,

util.NewNullableString(request.Description))  
if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to update book"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)  
return

}

if updatedAt == time.Date(1, time.January, 1, 0, 0, 0, 0, time.UTC)

{  
cause := "Book not found"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,  
util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)

return  
}

type updateBookResponse struct {  
UpdatedAt time.Time

}  
response = &updateBookResponse{

UpdatedAt: updatedAt,  
}

return  
}


Data Layer function for resource deletion will return number of  
aﬀected database rows (how many database rows are deleted). If

returned value is equal to zero (nothing has been deleted from  
database) we will return ErrResourceNotFound to client.

func deleteBook(ctx context.Context, bookID string) (err error) {

bookID = strings.TrimSpace(bookID)  
if bookID == "" {

cause := "Invalid value for bookID parameter"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)

return  
}

rowsAﬀected, err := data.DeleteBook(ctx, bookID)  
if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to delete book"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,  
err)

return

}

if rowsAﬀected == 0 {

cause := "Book not found"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,

util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)  
return

}

return

}


Last function, is most interesting of all book functions. We will

use one function for both operations (borrow and return) because

we just need to change book’s status. If somebody already  
borrowed the book, other members will not be able to borrow

the same book until the book is returned.

This is a reason why we only send bookID in request. If we have  
the option to send new book status, we can try to borrow already

borrowed book and that makes no sense. So we only need in

borrowOrReturnBook() to ﬁnd current book status and set the

opposite one.

In situation when book is in status we must diﬀerentiate two

situations:

Member who borrowed the book wants to return it.

Another member wants to borrow already borrowed book (in this  
case we should return error with appropriate message).

This can be accomplished with simple comparison. We need to  
compare ID of member who calls function with borrower ID. If

these two identiﬁers are the same, member wants to return book

and we can just change book’s status and remove borrower ID. If

identiﬁers are not the same, some other member tries to borrow  
unavailable book, and we just need to inform that user tath book

is not available.


Book statuses are deﬁned in const.go ﬁle inside values folder.  
Unknown status (value 0) will be considered as an error and

when Data Layer function GetBookStatus() returns this value

ErrResourceNotFound will be returned to client.

// Values for book status

const (

BookStatusUnknown = 0

BookStatusAvailable = 1  
BookStatusBorrowed = 2

)

When user borrows a book we will set his userID as a so the

librarian can know who borrowed which book. We can send this

ID in request body, but we already send the authorization token

in HTTP Request Header. Token is bounded with userID so we  
can use it to ﬁnd ID or user who requested operation.

Also, this will prevent users to borrow books for other users. If

user can send userID in HTTP Request Body he can send any ID  
and this is not desired behavior. When user returns book we will

set borrowerID to NULL and change status to available to

indicate that other users can borrow that book.

func borrowOrReturnBook(ctx context.Context, token string,

requestBody io.Reader) (err error) {

type borrowOrReturnBookRequest struct {  
BookID string

}


request := &borrowOrReturnBookRequest{}

err = json.NewDecoder(requestBody).Decode(request)

if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to decode JSON"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInvalidJSONBody,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)

return

}

request.BookID = strings.TrimSpace(request.BookID)

if request.BookID == "" {

cause := "Invalid value for bookID parameter"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeValidation,

util.ErrBadRequest, err)

return

}

status, err := data.GetBookStatus(ctx, request.BookID)

if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to get book status"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)

return

}

if status == values.BookStatusUnknown {

cause := "Book not found"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,

util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)


return

}

userUID, err := data.GetUserID(ctx, token)

if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to get userUID"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)

return

}

// if the book is borrowed by one who did not take the error

newStatus := values.BookStatusAvailable  
if status == values.BookStatusAvailable {

newStatus = values.BookStatusBorrowed

} else {

borrowerID := ""

borrowerID, err = data.GetBorrowerId(ctx, request.BookID)  
if err != nil {

cause := "Failed to get borrowerID"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)  
return

}

if borrowerID != userUID {

cause := "Book is not available"  
err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeEntityNotFound,

util.ErrResourceNotFound, err)

return

}


userUID = ""  
newStatus = values.BookStatusAvailable

}

err = data.ChangeBookStatus(ctx, request.BookID, newStatus,

util.NewNullableString(userUID))

if err != nil {  
cause := "Failed to change book status"

err = util.NewError(cause, util.ErrorCodeInternal, util.ErrInternal,

err)

return  
}

return

}

Core Layer is ready. Now we can deal with Data Layer.


Conclusion

We are familiar with all concepts that we need to the third layer

of our server application. We know diﬀerence between required  
and optional ﬁelds and how to handle them. Core Layer will  
handle business logic and prepare data for Data Layer.


Points to remember

Core Layer will handle business logic.

We should validate all required ﬁelds from HTTP Request.

Go package json will help us to convert JSON from HTTP

Request Body into Go struct.

We should return ErrResourceNotFound when function from Data  
Layer has no eﬀect.
